PSKEY_BDADDR

Number (psid) 0x0001 1
CategoryPSKLCB
Typebdaddr
DefaultPSKEY_BDADDR = { 42405 /* lap */, 91 /* uap */, 2 /* nap */}

Bluetooth address

The local device's Bluetooth address. This should be unique to this device. It is allocated during manufacturing.

The type bdaddr can be viewed as a uint16[4] array:

1st uint16: The top 8 bits of the LAP are in the bottom 8 bits of this word. The top 8 bits of this word must be zero. 2nd uint16: The lower 16 bits of the LAP 3rd uint16: The 8-bit UAP is in the bottom 8 bits of this word. The top 8 bits of this word must be zero. 4th uint16: 16-bit NAP

For example, the Bluetooth address 123456789abc is encoded as 0078, 9abc, 0056, 1234.

The default value of this key is one of QTIL's legal addresses: 00025b00a5a5.

As stated in the Bluetooth specification, LAP values from 9e8b00 up to, and including, 9e8b3f must not be used as this range is reserved for inquiry access codes (IACs).

Bluetooth module manufacturers must obtain their own block of addresses from the Bluetooth SIG/IEEE. If QTIL's experience is typical, these authorities define the NAP and UAP, allowing manufacturers to set the 24-bit LAP.


PSKEY_CLASSOFDEVICE

Number (psid) 0x0003 3
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeuint32
DefaultPSKEY_CLASSOFDEVICE = 0
Allowed Values
Minimum0
Maximum16777215

Class of device

The local device's default Bluetooth "Class of Device" or CoD.

Type bdcod is really a uint32. The class of device is a 24-bit value stored in a uint32; the highest byte must be zero.

This is the device's default class of device, used when the device boots. The device's class of device may subsequently be changed by an HCI command. The HCI command does not change the value stored under this PSKey.

The least significant two bits reveal the format of the other 22 bits. The only format currently defined is for where the two bits are zero:

Bits Content [1:0] Format Type (0) [7:2] Minor Dev Class (in the context of the Major Dev Class) [12:8] Major Dev Class [23:13] Major Service Class

At the time of writing, the firmware makes no use of this information.


PSKEY_DEVICE_DRIFT

Number (psid) 0x0004 4
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_DEVICE_DRIFT = 250
Allowed Values
Maximum250

Device drift

This PSKey holds the local device's radio timing drift in parts per million. The maximum value allowed by the Bluetooth specification is 250.

This value is used in LMP_timing_accuracy_res messages sent to peers, as described in Bluetooth version 1.1, LMP specification, section 5.2. It is also used in calculations in low power modes to decide for how long the radio on a slave device must be turned on in order to resynchronise with a remote master: reducing the value therefore allows power saving.

The default value is appropriate when BlueCore's internal low power oscillator is in use to maintain timing during low power modes, i.e. for the default setting of PSKEY_DEEP_SLEEP_STATE (DEEP_SLEEP_ALWAYS, value 1) and PSKEY_DEEP_SLEEP_USE_EXTERNAL_CLOCK (FALSE). The appropriate values for the various settings of these PSKeys are:

PSKEY_DEEP_SLEEP_STATE = NEVER or INACTIVE (0 or 2): set device drift to 20 ppm to reflect full Bluetooth clock accuracy.

PSKEY_DEEP_SLEEP_STATE = ALWAYS (1): if PSKEY_DEEP_SLEEP_USE_EXTERNAL_CLOCK is FALSE, set device drift to 250 ppm (default). If an external clock is in use, set device drift to the accuracy of that external clock.

PSKEY_DEEP_SLEEP_STATE = ALWAYS_ACCURATE (3): if PSKEY_DEEP_SLEEP_USE_EXTERNAL_CLOCK is TRUE, set device drift to the accuracy of the external slow clock.

Note: Some BlueCore7 and later parts can internally derive a slow clock from their fast clock and so the accuracy will be much better than 250 ppm. See comments in PSKEY_DEEP_SLEEP_STATE.


PSKEY_DEVICE_JITTER

Number (psid) 0x0005 5
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_DEVICE_JITTER = 10 Microseconds

Device jitter

This PSKey holds the local device's radio jitter in microseconds. (LMP v1.1, section 5.2.)

This value is used in LMP_timing_accuracy_res messages sent to peers. This is the only use for this PSKey.


PSKEY_MAX_ACLS

Number (psid) 0x000d 13
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_MAX_ACLS = 7
Allowed Values
Minimum0
Maximum40

Maximum ACL links

This PSKey holds the maximum number of concurrent ACL connections to other devices.

Links to remote devices use substantial amounts of RAM to maintain connection state, so this value should be kept low. It is advisable to trim this value to match the application, allowing any liberated RAM to be used elsewhere. The value must be reduced if the chip is running any of the higher layers of the Bluetooth stack because these take from the common supply of RAM.

On 23h and later firmware, reducing this key can allow the malloc space freed up to be put into larger pools for VM applications. See the descriptions of PSKEY_PMALLOC_PER_ACL and PSKEY_PMALLOC_BASE for more information. (This key has no direct effect on malloc usage for earlier firmware.)


PSKEY_MAX_SCOS

Number (psid) 0x000e 14
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_MAX_SCOS = 3
Allowed Values
Minimum0
Maximum3

Maximum SCO links

This PSKey holds the maximum number of SCO links to (all) other devices.

On 23h and later firmware, reducing this key can allow the malloc space freed up to be put into larger pools for VM applications. See the descriptions of PSKEY_PMALLOC_PER_SCO and PSKEY_PMALLOC_BASE for more information. (This key has no direct effect on malloc usage for earlier firmware.)

This value may be reduced to increase the buffer space available for ACL data: see the description of PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_ACL_PKT_LEN.


PSKEY_MAX_REMOTE_MASTERS

Number (psid) 0x000f 15
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_MAX_REMOTE_MASTERS = 2
Allowed Values
Minimum1
Maximum2

Maximum remote masters

This PSKey holds the local device's maximum number of remote piconet masters.

Connecting to multiple remote masters implies the use of scatternets. The current firmware supports one permanent remote master, plus a second remote master in a temporary state either for performing a remote name request or to connect by a role switch to become a slave.

See the description of PSKEY_ENABLE_MASTERY_WITH_SLAVERY.


PSKEY_ENABLE_MASTERY_WITH_SLAVERY

Number (psid) 0x0010 16
CategoryPSKLCB
TypeEnumTrueFalse
DefaultPSKEY_ENABLE_MASTERY_WITH_SLAVERY = TRUE
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
FALSE 0 False
TRUE 1 True

Support master and slave roles simultaneously

If this PSKey is set to TRUE (value 1) then the firmware is configured to support being a master of its own piconet at the same time as being a slave in one or more other piconets. This implies the use of scatternets.

This value is constrained by the value of the PSKey PSKEY_MAX_REMOTE_MASTERS.

The "barge-in" connection sequence (an existing master page-scans, it is paged by new a device, then the new device's link performs a master/slave switch) implies a temporary scatternet. This PSKey does not effect this behaviour.

See the description of PSKEY_MAX_REMOTE_MASTERS.

(Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to FALSE and TRUE.)


PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_ACL_PKT_LEN

Number (psid) 0x0011 17
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_ACL_PKT_LEN = 310
Allowed Values
Minimum1
Maximum512

Maximum HCI ACL packet length

This PSKey holds the maximum acceptable length, in bytes, of the data portion of HCI ACL data packets received from the host. This is reported by the HCI_Read_Buffer_Size HCI command as the HC_ACL_Data_Packet_Length value.

You may want to tune this value to obtain better device throughput. However, you must keep constant the product of the values of this key and of total number of host packets. Because this effectively reserves a block of the device's valuable RAM for use by the host.

For each SCO connection 1024 bytes of memory is reserved and if the max number of SCO connections (N)= PSKEY_MAX_SCOS is reduced by 1 from its firmware default, the effective total memory for ACL and fastpipe packets may be increased by 1024 bytes.

On parts that do not support ram reserve feature total number of host packets is taken from PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_ACL_PKTS. On these parts, if B = PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_ACL_PKTS, L = PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_ACL_PKT_LEN, and S is product B * L, when these keys have their firmware default values then the following four conditions must be satisfied if these keys are altered:

If the parts support EDR: 1. B * L <= S 2. B * L <= 3968 3. (B + 1) * L <= 4095 4. B <= 14

If the parts do not support EDR: 1. B * L <= S 2. B * L <= 1919 3. (B + 1) * L <= 2047 4. B <= 14

On parts that support ram reserve feature, total memory reserved for host (PSKEY_MMU_TRACKED_BYTES) is sum of buffers for ACL packets, buffers for fastpipe packets and SCO buffers. On these following are the parameters used to determine the max number of ACL packets. -> T = Tokens set by allocate_ram_reserve BCCMD -> B = HC_Total_Num_ACL_Data_Packets returned by HCI_Read_Buffer_Size HCI command (which includes T) + PSKEY_RESERVE_INIT_TOKENS -> L = PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_ACL_PKT_LEN -> N = PSKEY_MAX_SCOS

With above parameters following conditions must be satisfied if these keys are altered:

1. (B * L) + (N * 1024) <= PSKEY_MMU_TRACKED_BYTES (6236) 2. B * L <= 4032 3. (B + 1) * L <= 4095 4. B <= 14

Violating any of these conditions may cause the chip to crash or behave oddly. QTIL only supports configurations that meet all four of these conditions.


PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_SCO_PKT_LEN

Number (psid) 0x0012 18
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeuint8
DefaultPSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_SCO_PKT_LEN = 64
Allowed Values
Minimum1
Maximum128

Maximum HCI SCO packet length

This PSKey holds the maximum acceptable length, in bytes, of the data portion of HCI SCO data packets received from the host. This supports the HCI_Read_Buffer_Size HCI command.

You may want to tune this value to obtain better device throughput. However, you must keep constant the product of the values of this key and of PSKEY_H_HC_FC_MAX_SCO_PKTS because this effectively reserves a block of the device's valuable RAM for use by the host.

Only change this value after careful consideration: small values will heavily load the (host and) chip processor(s), and large values will normally increase audio latency.

PSKEY_LC_FC_BUFFER_LOW_WATER_MARK

Number (psid) 0x0015 21
CategoryPSKLCB
Typelc_fc_lwm
DefaultPSKEY_LC_FC_BUFFER_LOW_WATER_MARK = { 1536 /* junk_data */, 1792 /* assert_acl */, 2048 /* assert_l2cap */}

Flow control low water mark

This PS Key holds a set of values that control the assertion of flow control for data received from air.

The LC determines how much buffer memory has been promised to the host for host to air traffic, then it adds the safety margins set by this key and compares the result with the available free buffer memory. The result determines when and how the LC applies flow control for data received from air.

This PSKey holds an array of three values. Each value sets a behaviour threshold, measured in a number of bytes:

0: Received data is discarded and a NAK is returned 1: ACL flow control is asserted 2: L2CAP flow control is asserted


PSKEY_LC_MAX_TX_POWER

Number (psid) 0x0017 23
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeint16
DefaultPSKEY_LC_MAX_TX_POWER = 20 dBm
Allowed Values
Minimum-128 dBm
Maximum127 dBm

Maximum transmit power

This PSKey holds the device's maximum transmit power in dBm.

The firmware ensures the device never speaks more loudly than this value.

The firmware uses the highest value in the power table that is less than or equal to the requested default power.

Correct operation depends on having a valid power table - see PSKEY_LC_POWER_TABLE.

The maximum value depends on the Bluetooth module class:

Class 1: 0 to +20 dBm. Class 2: -6 to +4 dBm. Class 3: up to 0 dBm.

Unlike most PSKey values, this is a *signed* 16-bit integer.


PSKEY_TX_GAIN_RAMP

Number (psid) 0x001d 29
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_TX_GAIN_RAMP = 4096 Microseconds
Allowed Values
Minimum4 Microseconds
Maximum65535 Microseconds

Transmit gain ramp rate

This PSKey holds the device's transmitter gain ramp rate. It controls the power ramp-up at the start of a packet and ramp-down at the end of a packet.

QTIL recommends that this value is not modified from the default.

Bits [7:0] control the ramp rate. The normal range is between 0x04 and 0x3F. Values below 0x04 are out of spec and must not be used.

Bits [15:8] control the length of the unmodulated carrier between the end of the ramp and the start of the packet in microseconds.

The ramp rate value has different effects according to whether the module uses the chip's internal power amplifier or an external amplifier. (See PSKEY_TXRX_PIO_CONTROL.)

If the internal power amplifier is ramped then the microseconds taken to complete the ramp is (4*amplifier_setting)/ramp_rate.

If an external power amplifier is ramped then the microseconds taken to complete the ramp is (amplifier_setting)/ramp_rate

In both cases amplifier_setting is taken from the power table PSKEY_LC_ENHANCED_POWER_TABLE (PSKEY_LC_POWER_TABLE on older BlueCore devices where EDR is not supported).

The total time controlled by this PS key is ramp_time (calculated as above) + unmodulated_carrier_time


PSKEY_LC_FC_POOLS_LOW_WATER_MARK

Number (psid) 0x0020 32
CategoryPSKLCB
Typelc_fc_lwm
DefaultPSKEY_LC_FC_POOLS_LOW_WATER_MARK = { 20 /* junk_data */, 24 /* assert_acl */, 26 /* assert_l2cap */}

Flow control pool low water mark

This PSKey is similar to PSKEY_LC_FC_BUFFER_LOW_WATER_MARK, but describes numbers of available pool memory blocks.


PSKEY_LC_DEFAULT_TX_POWER

Number (psid) 0x0021 33
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeint16
DefaultPSKEY_LC_DEFAULT_TX_POWER = 4 dBm
Allowed Values
Minimum-128 dBm
Maximum127 dBm

Default transmit power

This PSKey holds the radio's default transmit power, measured in dBm. The chip uses this for page, inquiry and their scan responses. This is also the power used for new connections.

In 12.X builds the firmware uses the entry in the power table that is closest to this PSKey's value. If the two closest power tables are equidistant from this key's value then it is indeterminate which power table entry is used.

In 13.X and later builds the firmware uses the highest value in the power table that is less than or equal to the requested default power.

Correct operation depends on the device having a valid power table - see PSKEY_LC_POWER_TABLE.


PSKEY_LC_MAX_TX_POWER_NO_RSSI

Number (psid) 0x002d 45
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeint8
DefaultPSKEY_LC_MAX_TX_POWER_NO_RSSI = 4 dBm

Maximum transmit power when peer has no RSSI

This PSKey value is used after a connection is made, if it is found that a remote device does not support RSSI measurements or the local device does not support power control. The transmit power is lowered to correspond to the first entry in PSKEY_LC_POWER_TABLE whose power in dBm is less than or equal to the value of this PSKey.

According to the Bluetooth specification, a device may only transmit to a receiving device that does not support the necessary messaging for sending the power control messages using the rules for a class 2 or class 3 device, in other words, with a maximum transmit power of 4 dBm, hence the default value for this PSKey. This allows the default transmit power to be raised above 4 dBm without violating the specification.


PSKEY_LC_CONNECTION_RX_WINDOW

Number (psid) 0x002e 46
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_LC_CONNECTION_RX_WINDOW = 10

Receive window size during connections

The Bluetooth specification requires that a master or slave is sensitive to timing jitter of transmissions from the other side up to 10 microseconds while the two devices are connected. The value may be controlled by this PSKey.


PSKEY_BT_CLOCK_INIT

Number (psid) 0x0034 52
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeuint32
DefaultPSKEY_BT_CLOCK_INIT = 0
Allowed Values
Maximum268435455

Initial value of Bluetooth clock

This PSKey holds the value to which the Bluetooth clock is initialised at boot. The value 0 is standard; the only likely reason to alter this is for debugging non-QTIL devices known to encounter problems at certain clock values.

Historical note: before this key was introduced, QTIL devices initialised their Bluetooth clocks from the lower 28 bits of the Bluetooth address, i.e. the lower 4 bits of the UAP followed by the LAP.

PSKEY_LC_LOST_SYNC_SLOTS

Number (psid) 0x003b 59
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_LC_LOST_SYNC_SLOTS = 0
Allowed Values
Maximum32767

Time in ms for lost sync in low power modes

In low power modes, a device considers it has lost synchronisation with its peer if it fails to receive an expected transmission in one of the following circumstances:

- In sniff mode as a slave, during any sniff window when nothing is received.

- In sniff mode as a master, during any sniff window when the slave has been sent a POLL or a data packet and no reply has been received.

This PSKey specifies a value in baseband slots (units of 625 us) which must elapse since the last packet received from the remote device before the logic described above applies.


PSKEY_NO_CAL_ON_BOOT

Number (psid) 0x0042 66

Do not calibrate radio on boot

Set this PSKey to TRUE to cause the LC not to calibrate the radio at boot time. This means that the radio does not work until the key is set to false and the chip is rebooted. This key is intended to allow the use of a bootmode where the radio is disabled. For details on bootmodes, see the QTIL document "Understanding and Using Bootmodes", CS-101528-AN (previously numbered as bcore-an-019P), on the QTIL support website.

Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to FALSE and TRUE.

PSKEY_EDR_MODE_SWITCH_PIO

Number (psid) 0x0052 82
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeuint16
DefaultNone

EDR PA support on pio(x)

This PSKey asserts the PIO line specified, 0-15 if present. If the PSKey is not present it becomes a zero-length key with an attempt to read it failing. This fails the psget method and disables use of this key. If the PSKey is defined but the value is 0xffff, out of bounds, then the key does not set up a PIO line. Using this PSKey is intended to be the mode select line for an EDR power amp. The assertion method is in PSKEY EDR_SWITCH_MODE and will be either high to low or low to high.

If a PIO line is required for Tx enabling then you should use PSKEY_TXRX_PIO_CONTROL, pio pin 1 which asserts when transmitting.

PSKEY_LC_PEER_POWER_INCR_PERIOD

Number (psid) 0x0057 87
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeuint32
DefaultPSKEY_LC_PEER_POWER_INCR_PERIOD = 100000 Microseconds
Allowed Values
Minimum0 Microseconds
Maximum60000000 Microseconds

Peer transmit power control interval

This PSKey is the period, measured in microseconds, between attempts to increment the peer's transmit power.

Set this PSKey to zero to disable the periodic checks. This means the local device does not send messages concerning power management or channel quality driven data rate to the remote device. This PSKey is paired with decrement peer power period.

Type TIME is fundamentally a uint32. Value SECOND is 1000000. Value MILLISECOND is 1000.


PSKEY_LC_PEER_POWER_DECR_PERIOD

Number (psid) 0x0058 88
CategoryPSKLCB
Typeuint32
DefaultPSKEY_LC_PEER_POWER_DECR_PERIOD = 1000000 Microseconds
Allowed Values
Minimum100000 Microseconds
Maximum60000000 Microseconds

Peer transmit power control interval

This PSKey is the period, measured in microseconds, between attempts to decrement the peer's transmit power. The same interval is used for measurements of channel quality to support LMP channel quality driven data rate messages.

This PSKey is paired with the respective increment peer power period. This key has a minimum value of 100 ms. However it is disabled if the increment peer power period is set to 0. This means the local device does not send messages concerning peer power management.

Type TIME is fundamentally a uint32. Value SECOND is 1000000. Value MILLISECOND is 1000.


PSKEY_LC_HIGH_PRIORITY_SNIFF_TIMEOUTS

Number (psid) 0x0060 96
CategoryPSKLCB
TypeEnumTrueFalse
DefaultPSKEY_LC_HIGH_PRIORITY_SNIFF_TIMEOUTS = FALSE
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
FALSE 0 False
TRUE 1 True

High priority bandwidth for sniff timeout slots

This PSKey affects the algorithm that selects the value of Dsniff when negotiating sniff mode for an ACL connection. If no value is set or the value is FALSE, sniff timeout slots are not included in the calculation unless the quality of service for the connection is "guaranteed". If the value is TRUE, sniff timeout slots are always taken into account: this means that extra spacing is left in the air time schedule, where possible, to allow for a transmission to a slave during one iteration of the timeout slots.

This PSKey has no direct effect on the real-time scheduling of links in sniff mode, so it does not necessarily cause a master to address the slave in the timeout slots. A QoS setting of "guaranteed" for an ACL connection causes sniff timeout slots to be treated as high priority by the real-time scheduler. However, use this with caution because it can have a significant effect on the bandwidth available for other links.

Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to FALSE and TRUE.

PSKEY_LOCAL_SUPPORTED_FEATURES

Number (psid) 0x00ef 239
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeuint16[4]
DefaultPSKEY_LOCAL_SUPPORTED_FEATURES[ ] = { 65279, 65167, 65499, 34651}

Local supported features block

This PSKey holds a 4-element array of uint16s holding a bitfield that describes the features supported by the local device for page 0 of the device features bits mentioned in the LMP specification.

See PSKEY_LOCAL_SUPPORTED_FEATURES_PAGE_2 for the page 2 features. Note that PSKEY_LOCAL_SUPPORTED_FEATURES_PAGE_2 is only present in BlueCore firmware images which support page 2 features.

Coding matches the "coding of features" section in the LMP specification. The first byte of the coding of features is held in the lower byte of the first uint16, etc.

The key's default value gives the firmware's capabilities. Switching a bit from 0 to 1 does not create a missing capability.

This PSKey configures the local LM. If a feature is marked as provided by the default value, then clearing the key's bit turns off the corresponding functionality. For example, setting the Encryption bit to zero stops the local device supporting encryption.

The three "flow control lag" bits should be left at zero.

The order in 1.2 of the specification is:

First word, low to high (X => turned on in default config; (X) => turned on if supported by hardware;) On Bit Feature X 0 3-slot packets X 1 5-slot packets X 2 Encryption X 3 Slot offset X 4 Timing accuracy X 5 Master/slave switch X 6 Hold mode X 7 Sniff mode X 8 Reserved X 9 Power control requests X 10 Data rate driven by channel quality X 11 SCO link X 12 HV2 packets X 13 HV3 packets X 14 mu-law voice encoding X 15 A-law voice encoding

Second word X 0 CVSD X 1 Paging scheme X 2 Power control X 3 Transparent SCO data 4 } 5 } L2CAP flow control lag (our default = 0) 6 } [1.2 features from this point] X 7 Broadcast encryption 8 Reserved (Scatter mode) (X) 9 Enhanced Data Rate ACL 2 Mbps mode (X) 10 Enhanced Data Rate ACL 3 Mbps mode X 11 Enhanced inquiry scan X 12 Interlaced inquiry scan X 13 Interlaced page scan X 14 RSSI with inquiry results (X) 15 Extended SCO link --- EV3 packets

Third word (X) 0 Extended SCO link --- EV4 packets (X) 1 Extended SCO link --- EV5 packets 2 Reserved (Absence masks) X 3 AFH capable slave X 4 AFH classification slave 5 BR/EDR not supported 6 LE supported (Controller) (X) 7 3-slot Enhanced Data Rate ACL packets (X) 8 5-slot Enhanced Data Rate ACL packets X 9 Sniff Subrating X 10 Pause Encryption X 11 AFH capable master X 12 AFH classification master (X) 13 Enhanced Data Rate eSCO 2 Mbps mode (X) 14 Enhanced Data Rate eSCO 3 Mbps mode (X) 15 3-slot Enhanced Data Rate eSCO packets

Fourth word X 0 Extended Inquiry Response 1 Simultaneous LE and BR/EDR to same device capable (Controller) 2 Reserved X 3 Secure Simple Pairing X 4 Encapsulated PDU 5 Erroneous Data Reporting X 6 Non-flushable Packet Boundary Flag 7 Reserved X 8 Link Supervision Timeout Changed Event X 9 Inquiry Response TX Power Level X 10 Enhanced Power Control 11-14 Reserved X 15 Extended features [i.e. highest bit in feature mask]

PSKEY_HCI_NOP_DISABLE

Disable the HCI Command_Status event on boot

By default the BlueCore firmware sends an HCI command_status(NOP) event to the host shortly after booting. Although this is clearly allowed by the HCI specification it is known to crash some host stacks.

This PSKey provides a simple workaround: if this key is TRUE then this boot-time event is not emitted.

Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to FALSE and TRUE.

PSKEY_LM_TEST_SEND_ACCEPTED_TWICE

Number (psid) 0x00f6 246
CategoryPSKLMB
TypeEnumTrueFalse
DefaultPSKEY_LM_TEST_SEND_ACCEPTED_TWICE = FALSE
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
FALSE 0 False
TRUE 1 True

LM sends two LMP_accepted messages in test mode

The Bluetooth v1.1 specification does not ensure reliability of LMP traffic in test mode, because it does not differentiate test packets (which are unreliable) from LMP packets at the baseband level. This can lead to loss of LMP messages.

If this PSKey is set to TRUE, a slave in test mode sends the LMP_Accepted reply to a test control message twice. This increases the likelihood that the message will be received by the tester. (It does not guarantee it because, as the link manager does not operate in real time, there may be test messages in between the transmissions.)

Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to FALSE and TRUE.

Each time a unit pages a new device and it currently has active links, they are held for page timeout slots. If page timeout slots is greater than this PSKey value, this value is used a the maximum hold time. A value of zero indicates that holding around page is disabled.


PSKEY_AFH_ADAPTATION_RESPONSE_TIME

Number (psid) 0x00f8 248

Maximum0xbb80

LM period for AFH adaption

This PSKey sets the interval between successive channel classification updates (and hence channel map adaptations) for an AFH enabled master. The period is measured in baseband slots (625us), and is between 1 and 30 seconds.

The slave classification intervals sent in the LMP_channel_classfication_req message are derived from this value: AFH_max_interval = this_value AFH_min_interval = this_value / 2


PSKEY_AFH_OPTIONS

Number (psid) 0x00f9 249
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_AFH_OPTIONS = 0x0057

Options to configure AFH

This PSKey allows you to configure AFH. The bits are not restricted to classification, as follows: Bit 0 enable RSSI classification Bit 1 enable PLR classification Bit 2 enable use of combo information in classification Bit 3 <reserved> Bit 4 enable hysterisis of the classifications from slaves Bit 5 disable RSSI classification with "low power" links Bit 6 enable extended RSSI classification with "low power" links, this enables the time period for RSSI classification to be PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_LP_RUN_PERIOD.

RSSI - BlueCore makes signal strength measurements of channels not being used by the Bluetooth link when the radio would otherwise be idle. In ideal radio conditions, this increases the power consumption during a connection. However, it has the advantage that it makes Bluetooth a good neighbour; it identifies and avoids other users of the ISM band even if they are not causing problems for Bluetooth operation and can return channels to use when the interferer is no longer present. Power consumption can be reduced with interference present as there is a reduced need for message retransmissions. QTIL recommends that RSSI is enabled.

When all links are "low power", power consumption for RSSI classification can be reduced by not performing RSSI scans (setting Bit 5), or performing them less regularly (setting Bit 6 and setting PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_LP_RUN_PERIOD larger than PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_RUN_PERIOD). "Low power" links are in sniff with a period of more than 128 slots. (This value was chosen to distinguish sniff periods used in HID devices from those used by, for example, idle headsets.)

Note: A link is never considered to be "low power" if it has a SCO or eSCO link associated with it, so that adding an (e)SCO link to a sniffed link immediately restarts or speeds up classification when using Bits 5 or 6 of this PSKey.

PLR - Dropped packets and bit error rates for FEC encoded headers and payloads are used to estimate the interference for each of the channels being used. This gives priority to channels that are degrading the Bluetooth performance. As mentioned above, it does not identify other users of the ISM band unless they are corrupting Bluetooth packets, and it does not rapidly detect the removal of an interferer on a channel being avoided. Additionally, BlueCore can only apply this method when it is master of the link.

To use AFH functionality to avoid interference, at least one device in the link must include a classifier.


PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_RUN_PERIOD

Number (psid) 0x00fa 250
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_AFH_RSSI_RUN_PERIOD = 475
Allowed Values
Minimum50
Maximum65535

AFH RSSI reading period

This PSKey sets the period with which the LC schedules an RSSI classification. When this period has passed, and there is a gap in Bluetooth activity, the Bluetooth radio is used as a spectrum analyser to read the RSSI on all Bluetooth channels. These values are averaged and decay slowly.

Note: Bit 6 of PSKEY_AFH_OPTIONS allows a longer period to be used for links in sniff. See the descriptions of PSKEY_AFH_OPTIONS and PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_LP_RUN_PERIOD for more information.

The value of this PSKey is in units of ms.


PSKEY_AFH_REENABLE_CHANNEL_TIME

Number (psid) 0x00fb 251
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_AFH_REENABLE_CHANNEL_TIME = 0x0fa0
Allowed Values
Minimum0x00fa
Maximum0xffff

AFH good channel adding time

This PSKey determines the amount of time it takes for a channel that was marked as bad to be marked as good again (when there is no further information about that channel). The time is approximately Key * 40 milliseconds. The actual time varies, as reintroduction is deliberately randomised. The fastest possible time is 25% of this time.

In the presence of broadband signals, the time to mark the channels affected by these signals is increased. This reduces the chance of further interference from the broadband source - which may be caused by beacons or varying data transfer on the broadband signal.

Channels are typically marked as unknown much sooner than this. AFH selection algorithms may use this as a hint to use the channel sooner.

The value of this PSKey is in units of 40 ms.


PSKEY_NO_DROP_ON_ACR_MS_FAIL

Number (psid) 0x00fc 252
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeboolean
DefaultPSKEY_NO_DROP_ON_ACR_MS_FAIL = true
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
false 0
true 1

Complete link if acr barge-in role switch refused

If the Role parameter to the HCI Accept_Connection_Request (acr) command is 0x00 it requires the local device to become master of the link. This means requesting the existing (paging) master to perform a role switch, and only completing the connection if the switch is performed. The link is dropped if the request to perform a role switch is refused. You can configure the HCI Set_Event_Filter command to achieve the same behaviour without involving the host via Connection_Request.

Set the PSKey to TRUE to alter this behaviour: if the Role parameter is 0x00 then it is treated as advice - the local device requests the paging master to perform a role switch, but the link is not dropped if this is refused. The behaviour of the event filter is similarly adjusted. No attempt is made to hide a failure to switch. For example, no Role_Change event is sent to the host.

This PSKey attempts to fix situations where both devices insist on being master. However, it changes the behaviour of HCI, so there is no guarantee that a given host stack will behave correctly. You must determine the correct system operation.

If this PSKey is FALSE, the firmware provides the normal HCI behaviour.

Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to FALSE and TRUE.


PSKEY_LOCAL_SUPPORTED_COMMANDS

Number (psid) 0x0106 262
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeuint16[9..34]
DefaultPSKEY_LOCAL_SUPPORTED_COMMANDS[ ] = { 65535, 1023, 65486, 65535, 65535, 65535, 4083, 65256, 63295, 65411, 28, 4, 63329, 65535, 14463, 65472, 61695, 63495, 1}

Local supported commands

This PSKey holds a large bitfield (in little-endian format) that describes which HCI commands are supported by the host controller. The Host finds out this information by trying the command. The Host Controller then returns with "Unknown HCI Command", but some Hosts might prefer to try this command first.

The result returned by this command does not change after the Host Controller has booted. Sometimes it is not possible for the Host Controller to perform some operations (eg. insufficient resources or not having a link of the correct type). This command still implies that the commands are available; if the Host tries such a command the Host Controller should return a different status message than "Unknown HCI Command".

PSKEY_DEVICE_NAME

Number (psid) 0x0108 264
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeunicode_string
DefaultPSKEY_DEVICE_NAME = """"
Allowed Values
Maximum string length40 octets

Local device's "user friendly" name

This PSKey holds the local device's default "user friendly" name, used by the HCI Read_Local_Name and Change_Local_Name commands and by LMP_name_req/LMP_name_res transactions.

When the firmware is booted, the device's name is taken from this PSKey. However, if the local host alters the local device's name, by calling the HCI Change_Local_Name command, then the new name is held in RAM. Subsequent requests to read the device's name take from the RAM store, not from this PSKey. The PSKey's value only becomes visible again after the firmware reboots.

The Bluetooth v1.1 HCI specification requires the device's default name to be ""; an empty string. The default (psrom) value of this PSKey is "QTIL - bc3" or similar. Therefore, the psrom value does not meet the HCI specification. If this PSKey is set to hold nothing, i.e., no uint16s are stored under the PSKey, then the HCI default value is obtained.

Over HCI and LMP the name is passed as a sequence of UTF-8 octets. Because the PS stores data in arrays of uint16s, the name is packed in this PSKey, two octets per uint16. This packing is important when the PS store is small, notably where the PS is held in EEPROM.

Working from the start of the device's name, the first character is stored in the lower octet of the PSKey's first uint16, the second character in the upper octet of the first uint16, etc. If the name is an odd number of characters then the upper octet of the last uint16 is '\0'.

This PSKey can hold a maximum of 20 uint16s, limiting the default device name to 40 octets. The behaviour is undefined in this PSKey holds more than 20 uint16s. (This size constraint does not apply to a name written via the HCI Change_Local_Name command.)

The default name for BlueCore3 chips is "QTIL - bc3"; when packed this becomes {0x5343, 0x2052, 0x202d, 0x6362, 0x0033}.

This PSKey is used from (HCI) 18.X builds. HCI 17.X and earlier builds use PSKEY_LOCAL_NAME0 -> PSKEY_LOCAL_NAME17 and PSKEY_LOCAL_NAME_LENGTH.


PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_THRESHOLD

Number (psid) 0x0109 265
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_AFH_RSSI_THRESHOLD = 0x0400

AFH RSSI threshold

This PSKey holds a value that controls the threshold of the entire RSSI classification algorithm. If the standard deviation of the power in the band is below this level then the device assumes that the entire band is clear and adapts its channel ratings accordingly.


PSKEY_LM_CASUAL_SCAN_INTERVAL

Number (psid) 0x010a 266
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeuint16
DefaultNone

Scan interval in slots for casual scanning

If this PSKey is set and is non-zero, `casual scanning' is enabled. The value then gives a maximum interval in slots between page and inquiry scans.

In this mode, page and inquiry scans are not necessarily performed with the frequency of the intervals set via HCI_write_inquiry_scan_activity and HCI_write_page_scan_activity. If the chip is active at any point after the interval specified over HCI since the previous scan, it performs the scan of the appropriate type. If it does not become active within PSKEY_LM_CASUAL_SCAN_INTERVAL slots after the previous scan, it performs the scan at that point.

On chips prior to BlueCore3-ROM, casual wakeup relies on the chip being woken up for some other reason, either by the host or due to an internal timer.

Casual wakeup is most useful on hardware starting with BlueCore3-ROM. This contains support for waking the chip from deep sleep if the host provides a clock. In this case, if the host provides a clock at any time after the normal scan interval, the chip wakes to perform the scan in synchronisation with the host. Otherwise, it waits until PSKEY_LM_CASUAL_SCAN_INTERVAL slots have elapsed and wake anyway.

For this reason you should only set this PSKey when the host provides a clock input that goes low when the chip enters deep sleep. Otherwise there is a significant peformance impact as the chip is woken unnecessarily.

On chips from BlueCore3-ROM but before BlueCore4-ROM, the key is also only useful with host transports that do not use PSKEY_UART_SLEEP_TIMEOUT as the chip stays awake for that period if woken by a host clock. This is likely to be a source of considerable inefficiency. On chips from BlueCore4-ROM, the firmware distinguishies wakeups caused by the presence of the host clock from those caused by data on the UART, so this restriction does not apply.

Casual scanning is not used in continuous page scan, because in this case the chip never becomes inactive.

If casual scanning is in use, the link manager reports the scan repetition mode based on the larger of the page scan interval and the casual scan interval.


PSKEY_AFH_MIN_MAP_CHANGE

Number (psid) 0x010b 267
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeuint16[2]
DefaultPSKEY_AFH_MIN_MAP_CHANGE[ ] = { 2, 4}

The minimum amount to change an AFH map by

This PSKey defines the minimum amount by which the device changes a channel map. If the channel map is rapidly changing by only a very small amount then the device prefers not to send too many channel map changes of classification reports.

The first number is the number of channels that must have got worse to cause the device to send a message. The second number is the number of channels that must have improved to cause the device to send a message. Having the second number bigger than the first means that the device will send messages more frequently as things become worse (as it knocks out more channels). The device then only adds channels back in as things become better.

Setting either value to zero disables this feature - the device sends the channel map message whenever the channel map changes.

The 'all good' channel map is a special case: the device always sends this.


PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_LP_RUN_PERIOD

Number (psid) 0x010c 268
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_AFH_RSSI_LP_RUN_PERIOD = 5000
Allowed Values
Minimum50
Maximum65535

AFH RSSI reading period when in low power mode

The value of this PSKey is used in place of PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_RUN_PERIOD when all Bluetooth links are in a "low power" mode (see the description of PSKEY_AFH_OPTIONS for the definition of "low power"). Therefore, this key is normally much larger than PSKEY_AFH_RSSI_RUN_PERIOD to reduce power when links are in sniff.

This period is enabled by Bit 6 in PSKEY_AFH_OPTIONS. The value of this PSKey is in unit of ms.

The HCI and LMP version reported locally

This PSKey holds the HCI_version and LMP_version information reported to the local host when the host sends HCI_Read_Local_Version_Information. The HCI_Version is the top 8 bits, the LMP_Version is the bottom 8 bits.


PSKEY_LMP_REMOTE_VERSION

PSKEY_ERROR_CODE_LTADDR_EXHAUSTION

Number (psid) 0x0114 276
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeuint8
DefaultPSKEY_ERROR_CODE_LTADDR_EXHAUSTION = 0x09

Error code to be used when we run out of LT_ADDRs

The BlueTooth specification is not clear about which HCI error code should be used if a device runs out of LT addresses when it has fewer than the maximum allowed number of ACL connections (see PSKEY_MAX_ACLS). This can happen if a connection is lost without a clean disconnect taking place; the device then reserves the address that the connection was using for some amount of time.

If an attempt is made to create an ACL connection, for example to perform a remote name request or service search, when the device has fewer than PSKEY_MAX_ACLS existing ACL connections but has no available LT_ADDRs, the value of this PSKey is returned in the HCI command complete event.

Note: The value of this key does not get validated at all. However, QTIL recommends only using the following values:

- Connection Limit Exceeded (0x09) This is the same error code as that returned if PSKEY_MAX_ACLS is exceeded. Because this value is ambiguous, it is unsuitable for some hosts.

- Memory Capacity Exceeded (0x07) This error code is also returned if the device runs out of RAM and suggests to the host that the attempt should succeed if the host first performs an operation that frees up some RAM. As freeing RAM does not help in the case of LT_ADDR exhaustion, this error code is misleading and so unsuitable for some hosts.

- Connection Rejected due to Limited Resources (0x0d) This error code is meant to suggest that the connection has been rejected by the remote device but, in this case, the connection has been rejected by the local device so this error code is not correct.

- Unspecified Error (0x1f) The most suitable of the defined error codes but not specific to this error condition.


PSKEY_SP_ENABLE_ECC_KEY_CHANGES

Number (psid) 0x0115 277
CategoryPSKLMB
TypeEnumTrueFalse
DefaultPSKEY_SP_ENABLE_ECC_KEY_CHANGES = FALSE
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
FALSE 0 False
TRUE 1 True

Enable ECC key protection by changing keys

When enabled, this key will cause the BlueCore device to change the public/private keypair intermittently in line with guidance from the Bluetooth specification. This provides protection against some forms of attacks on the DH key exchange procedure.

The ECC key is protected by additional mechanisms irrespective of the value of this key. For persistent Out-Of-Band pairing data, this key must be set to FALSE.

Enabling both this key and PSKEY_SP_STORE_GENERATED_ECC_KEY is not a valid configuration (the key cannot both persist and regularly change).


PSKEY_SP_STORE_GENERATED_ECC_KEY

Number (psid) 0x0116 278
CategoryPSKLMB
TypeEnumTrueFalse
DefaultPSKEY_SP_STORE_GENERATED_ECC_KEY = FALSE
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
FALSE 0 False
TRUE 1 True

Store ECC keys genereted during Simple Pairing

If this PSKey is set to TRUE then any ECC keys generated during Simple Pairing are written into PSKEY_SP_ECC_KEY. For persistent Out-Of-Band pairing data, this key must be set to TRUE.

Enabling both this key and PSKEY_SP_ENABLE_ECC_KEY_CHANGES is not a valid configuration (the key cannot both persist and regularly change).


PSKEY_SP_ECC_KEY

Number (psid) 0x0117 279
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeuint16[ ]
DefaultNone

ECC P192 Key Pair

This PSKey sets a P192 ECC Simple Pairing Key Pair. If this PSKey is set, BlueCore will not generate a key pair but instead use the one provided in this PSKey. The valid format is as follows: [private key length][private key][public key X length][public key X] [public key Y length][public key Y]

where X and Y are the first and second halves of the public key respectively. The length fields specify the number of used words in the respective key field (i.e. after stripping MS zero words) - The actual size of the fields are fixed.

The keys should be split into 16-bit words and programmed least significant word first.

For example, a 32-bit key: 0791 5f86

becomes: 5f86 0791

It is important that this template must be followed exactly otherwise the PSKey will be disregarded with no warning or error message returned.

Warning: Setting this key to the debug values as specified by the Bluetooth Core Specification is considered insecure as an active/passive attacker that has access to the debug private key can proceed to eavesdrop on all encrypted traffic between the hosts and perform a Man-in-the-Middle attack.

This key should only be altered on the advice of QTIL.

If PSKEY_SP_STORE_GENERATED_ECC_KEY is set to TRUE then any generated key pairs will be written to this PSKey.

There is a PSKEY_SP_ECC_P256_KEY which is the equivalent of this PSKey but for storage of P256 key pairs. The two keys are not dependent on one another.

Sets the rate for BLE version exchange

This PSKey determines the likelihood of version exchange being done automatically when Bluetooth Low Energy (BLE) connections are made. PSKEY_DEFAULT_BLE_FEATURES

Number (psid) 0x011c 284
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeuint16[4]
DefaultPSKEY_DEFAULT_BLE_FEATURES[ ] = { 16703, 0, 0, 0}

BLE local supported features

This PSKey contains a 4-element array of uint16s holding a bitfield that describes the Bluetooth Low Energy (BLE) features supported by the local device.

Currently only the first word is being used (from the LSB upwards) as defined in the BLE feature set as per the specification. The remaining bits are currently unused.

The PSKey's default value gives the firmware's capabilities. Switching a bit from 0 to 1 does not create a missing capability.

This PSKey configures the local LM. If a feature is marked as provided by the default value, then clearing the PSKey's bit turns off the corresponding functionality. For example, setting the Encryption bit to zero stops the local device supporting encryption.

The bit order as per the specification is:

First word, low to high Bit Feature 0 LE Encryption 1 Connection Parameters Request Procedure 2 Extended Reject Indication 3 Slave-initiated Features Exchange 4 LE Ping 5 Data Length Extension (DLE) [7:6] RFU 8 2Mbit PHY 9 Stable Modulation Index [13:10] RFU 14 LE Channel Selection Algorithm #2 15 RFU

Second word [15:0] RFU

Third word [15:0] RFU

Fourth word [15:0] RFU

CategoryPSKLMB
Typeuint8
DefaultPSKEY_BLE_FEATURE_REQ_RATE = 10
Allowed Values

Maximum30

Sets the rate for a BLE master to send an autonomous feature request

This PSKey determines the likelihood of feature exchange being done automatically when Bluetooth Low Energy (BLE) connections are made. If the value of the key is n then feature exchange is done automatically every n connections.

If set to zero, no automatic feature exchange takes place.

PSKEY_AFH_BLE_MIN_MAP_CHANGE

Number (psid) 0x011f 287
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeuint16[2]
DefaultPSKEY_AFH_BLE_MIN_MAP_CHANGE[ ] = { 2, 4}

The minimum amount to change a BLE AFH map by

This PSKey defines the minimum amount that the device changes the BLE channel map when it is the master of a connection. If the channel map is rapidly changing by only a very small amount then the device prefers not to send too many channel map updates to the slave.

The first value is the number of channels that must have worsened to cause the device to send a message. The second value is the number of channels that must have improved to cause the device to send a message. PSKEY_BLE_SLAVE_ALLOW_BREDR

Allow BLE slaves to partake in BR/EDR activities.

This PSKey controls internal link manager behaviour. Do not change it except on specific advice from QTIL. This PSKey exists to disable specific BLE and BR/EDR role combinations that are prohibited by the Generic Access Profile. Enabling this PSKey will allow the prohibited role combinations, which will potentially allow BLE links to clash with BR/EDR links with unpredictable results and possible loss of throughput.

PSKEY_ENABLE_CSB_NEW_AFH_MAP_EVENT

Number (psid) 0x0125 293
CategoryPSKLMB
TypeEnumTrueFalse
DefaultPSKEY_ENABLE_CSB_NEW_AFH_MAP_EVENT = FALSE
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
FALSE 0 False
TRUE 1 True

Control reporting of new AFH ch map to Host

When a BlueCore device is set up as a Connectionless Slave Broadcast transmitter or receiver, this PSKEY controls whether the BlueCore device periodically calculates an AFH channel map and reports it to the Host if it is sufficiently different from the existing map.

The periodicity of AFH map calculation is specified in PSKEY_AFH_ADAPTATION_RESPONSE_TIME and the amount of change necessary for the map to be considered new is specified in PSKEY_AFH_CSB_MIN_MAP_CHANGE.

If this PSKEY is set to TRUE, the BlueCore reports the new channel map to the Host via an HCI event.

If this PSKEY is set to FALSE, no such event is generated.


PSKEY_AFH_CSB_MIN_MAP_CHANGE

Number (psid) 0x0126 294
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeuint16[2]
DefaultPSKEY_AFH_CSB_MIN_MAP_CHANGE[ ] = { 2, 4}

Minimum amount to consider a CSB AFH map new

When a BlueCore device is set up as a Connectionless Slave Broadcast transmitter or receiver, this PSKEY defines the minimum amount with which the calculated channel map should differ from the existing map in order for it to be considered 'new'. When the calculated channel map is considered new, its availability is notified to the Host depending upon the value of PSKEY_ENABLE_CSB_NEW_AFH_MAP_EVENT.

The first value is the number of channels that must have worsened to cause the device to treat this as a new channel map. The second value is the number of channels that must have improved to cause the device to treat this as a new channel map. Having the second number bigger than the first means that the device sends notifications to the Host more frequently as things become worse (as it knocks out more channels), and less frequently as things become better (minimising false positives).

Setting either value to zero disables this feature. The device sends notification to the Host every time the channel map changes.


PSKEY_BLE_MIN_ADV_INTERVAL

Number (psid) 0x0127 295
CategoryPSKLMB
Typeuint8
DefaultPSKEY_BLE_MIN_ADV_INTERVAL = 32
Allowed Values
Minimum32
Maximum160

Non-connectable minimum advertising interval

This key sets the minimum advertising interval (in slots) to be effectively used for non-connectable advertising type only.

This PSKey permits to re-configure the minimum advertising interval in the range 20ms to 100ms (i.e. 32 to 160 slots) and only applicable for non-connectable advertising type. The value provided is used as minimum advertising interval threshold that HCI_LE_Set_Advertising_Parameters command parameters must govern to.

In order to efficiently broadcast information in a connectionless mode, a QTIL device can do non-connectable advertising at high duty cycle for short bursts using this PSKey.


PSKEY_BCSP_LM_PS_BLOCK

Number (psid) 0x0192 402
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
TypeBCSP_LM_PS_BLOCK
DefaultPSKEY_BCSP_LM_PS_BLOCK = { 1 /* mode */, 0 /* sync_retries */, 250 /* tshy */} Milliseconds

BCSP link establishment block

This PSKey configures the BCSP link establishment protocol. This is only used if BCSP is used over the chip's UART.

The configuration uses a structure of type BCSP_LM_PS_BLOCK where fields are:

uint16 mode 0: disable link establishment. 1: enable link establishment. 2: enable passive-start link establishment. This option causes the link establishment engine on the device to emit no messages until it receives traffic from the host.

uint16 sync_retries Support for this argument has been removed.

It used to set the number of sync packets emitted before the BCSP link establishment engine gave up and marked the link as dead. A value of zero meant "don't stop." The BCSP link establishment engine now always behaves as if the value is zero.

uint16 tshy The Tshy value in milliseconds.

This is the interval in which the BCSP link establishment engines send "sync" messages. This value is also used by the BCSP link establishment engine's Tconf timer.

For more information see QTIL document "BCSP Link Establishment Protocol", CS-101681-SP.


PSKEY_HOSTIO_PROTOCOL_INFO0

Number (psid) 0x0194 404
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
TypePROTOCOL_INFO
DefaultPSKEY_HOSTIO_PROTOCOL_INFO0 = { 0 /* max_tx_payload_size */, false /* reliable_stream */, 0 /* priority */, 0 /* unused */}

Host transport channel 0 settings (BCSP ACK)

This PSKey configures the protocol that flows over BCSP channel 0.

The host transport subsystem provides 16 channels, each of which is configured by a PROTOCOL_INFO struct held in the persistent store.

BCSP channel 0 is dedicated to signalling between BCSP stacks, specifically to carry message acknowledgements. Therefore, it is not available as a channel to carry user messages through BCSP, and is used by the BCSP host transport only.

While channel 0 is not available, the structure described below is used for the other channels in the host transport subsystem.

The type PROTOCOL_INFO has the following fields:

uint16 max_tx_payload_size - The maximum size in bytes of BCSP payload sent to the host. For ACL and SCO the actual maximum size will be the lower of the value from PS and the value indicated to the BlueCore device in the host's HOST_BUFFER_SIZE command, if one has been received. These values are checked at run time against the size of hardware buffer allocated.

int:1 reliable_stream - TRUE (bit value of 1) if the protocol uses BCSP's reliable stream.

int:4 priority - A value between 0 and 7. Lower values have higher priority. The priority is used by the device's BCSP scheduler when deciding what data to send to the host.

int:1 enabled - TRUE (bit value of 1) if the protocol is enabled. The current design of the firmware code requires each protocol to be enabled explicitly internally by the firmware, so this flag should always be FALSE.

The last three fields are packed as bitfields in the second word, as shown below:

Bits [9:0] Unused (second byte plus lower 2 bits) 10 enabled [14:11] priority 15 reliable_stream

For more information, see QTIL document "BCSP Channel Allocation", CS-101680-SP.


PSKEY_HOSTIO_PROTOCOL_INFO1

Number (psid) 0x0195 405
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
TypePROTOCOL_INFO
DefaultPSKEY_HOSTIO_PROTOCOL_INFO1 = { 256 /* max_tx_payload_size */, false /* reliable_stream */, 0 /* priority */, 0 /* unused */}

Host transport channel 1 settings (BCSP-LE)

This PSKey configures the protocol that flows over BCSP channel 1. This channel carries BCSP link establishment if BCSP is used. This channel is used only when BCSP is the host transport, however the max_tx_packet_size and priority settings for this protocol are also applied to non DFU USB traffic transmitted over the Control endpoint when BlueCore is using the USB host interface.

The protocol is configured with a PROTOCOL_INFO structure. The structure is described with PSKEY_HOSTIO_PROTOCOL_INFO0.


PSKEY_HOSTIO_PROTOCOL_INFO2

Number (psid) 0x0196 406
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
TypePROTOCOL_INFO
DefaultPSKEY_HOSTIO_PROTOCOL_INFO2 = { 256 /* max_tx_payload_size */, true /* reliable_stream */, 3 /* priority */, 0 /* unused */}

Host transport channel 2 settings (BCCMD)

This PSKey configures the protocol that flows over host transport channel 2. This channel carries BCCMD (BlueCore Command Interpreter Channel) - the host to chip "private channel." This channel is available for all host transports.

The protocol is configured with a PROTOCOL_INFO structure. The structure is described with PSKEY_HOSTIO_PROTOCOL_INFO0.

PSKEY_HOSTIO_UART_RESET_TIMEOUT

Number (psid) 0x01a4 420
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
Typeuint32
DefaultPSKEY_HOSTIO_UART_RESET_TIMEOUT = 0 Microseconds
Allowed Values
Minimum0 Microseconds
Maximum10000000 Microseconds

UART reset counter timeout

This PSKey configures the UART's reset counter timeout in microseconds.

If the UART's receive data line is held low for this period then the chip's (hardware) resets itself. Accuracy is +/- 30%, so it is important to specify to the nearest microsecond.

If this value is zero then the feature is disabled.

Values between 1 and 999 are treated as zero.

This feature only works with the UART host transports: BCSP, H4, H5 and VM access to the UART.

If PSKEY_HOSTIO_UART_RESET_TIMEOUT is set then make sure PSKEY_UART_BITRATE or PSKEY_UART_BAUDRATE is set to a non-zero value. Otherwise the chip will try autobaud detect and it will not move to deep sleep until UART_BREAK is removed.

Type TIME is fundamentally a uint32.


PSKEY_HOSTIO_USE_HCI_EXTN

Number (psid) 0x01a5 421
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
TypeEnumTrueFalse
DefaultPSKEY_HOSTIO_USE_HCI_EXTN = FALSE
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
FALSE 0 False
TRUE 1 True

Use hci_extn to route non-hci channels

If the system is using BCSP and this PSKey is FALSE then the non-HCI BCSP channels (currently 7: BCCMD, HQ, 4 higher layer access libs and the VM's channel) are routed via their BCSP channels. Otherwise, they are routed via hci_extn, described in QTIL document "BlueCore HCI Extensions", CS-101682-SP, available from the QTIL support website.

If the system is using H4 or USB then these channels are always routed over hci_extn. For Hostio over Transaction Bus, this is controlled by PSKEY_HOSTIO_TBUS_USE_HCI_EXTN.

Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to FALSE and TRUE.


PSKEY_HOSTIO_USE_HCI_EXTN_CCFC

Number (psid) 0x01a6 422
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
TypeEnumTrueFalse
DefaultPSKEY_HOSTIO_USE_HCI_EXTN_CCFC = FALSE
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
FALSE 0 False
TRUE 1 True

Use command-complete flow control for hci_extn

If the system is using hci_extn to carry the non-HCI channels (see the descriptions of PSKEY_HOSTIO_USE_HCI_EXTN and PSKEY_HOSTIO_TBUS_USE_HCI_EXTN) and this key is TRUE then the chip emits an "hci command complete event" for each HCI manufacturer extension command.

Set this PSKey to TRUE so that the host->chip data flow through hci_extn fits most closely to the HCI flow control model. However, this also means the hci_extn channel has glacial performance. If this is FALSE then the hci_extn traffic depends (only) on the tunnelled channels' own flow control mechanisms.

Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to FALSE and TRUE.


PSKEY_HOSTIO_HCI_EXTN_PAYLOAD_SIZE

Number (psid) 0x01a7 423
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_HOSTIO_HCI_EXTN_PAYLOAD_SIZE = 255
Allowed Values
Minimum2
Maximum255

Maximum hci_extn payload size

If the system is using hci_extn to carry the non-HCI channels (see the descriptions of PSKEY_HOSTIO_USE_HCI_EXTN and PSKEY_HOSTIO_TBUS_USE_HCI_EXTN) then this value specifies the maximum size of the HCI event payloads when primitives on non-HCI channels are fragmented. This PSKey value is the size of the HCI event payload, where one byte is used for the HCI-extn payload descriptor. Therefore each fragment is, at most, one byte less than this value. The minimum value for this PS value is therefore 2, though such a low value is likely to give extremely poor performance. The maximum value is 255 (because the length field in the HCI event header is only 8 bits wide).

Set this value lower than the maximum expected payload size to force hci_extn to fragment. This can be good when the host connection carries time-critical traffic, notably SCO.


PSKEY_BCSP_LM_CNF_CNT_LIMIT

Number (psid) 0x01aa 426
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_BCSP_LM_CNF_CNT_LIMIT = 20

BCSP link establishment conf message count

The value of this PSKey is only used if PSKEY_USE_OLD_BCSP_LE is set to TRUE.

Most early versions of the BCSP Link Establishment engine detected only that the peer BCSP stack had started - this is what the protocol was designed to do, as the protocol was written to support a host and BlueCore01 on the same circuit board (in a cell phone).

Later versions of the BCSP Link Establishment engine use an extension that allows the local engine to spot when the peer engine restarts - typically the case when the peer reboots.

To use this feature both sides of the BCSP link must support this extension and the value of this variable must be non-zero. This variable sets the number of "conf" messages emitted by the local engine, as described in QTIL document "BCSP Link Establishment Protocol", CS-101681-SP, available from the QTIL support website.


PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM

Number (psid) 0x01ab 427
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
TypeEnumTrueFalse
DefaultPSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM = FALSE
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
FALSE 0 False
TRUE 1 True

Map SCO over PCM

The following options are available to route SCO data over PCM port:

- Use the BCCMD command MAP_SCO_PCM to cause the next HCI Add_SCO_Connection command to route to a PCM port.

- Use this PSKey.

- [unified-25 onwards] Use streams interface.

If this PSKey is TRUE and PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_CODEC is FALSE then all attempts to open SCO connections map to one of the PCM ports based on PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM_SLOT.

In HCI 14.X builds, only a single SCO stream can flow over the BlueCore2-EXT's PCM port.

In HCI 15.X and later builds which do not have facility of PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM_SLOT, set the PSKey to cause all attempts to open SCO channels to run over *the first* PCM channel in the PCM port. (The clock settings in PSKEY_PCM_CONFIG32 determine whether the PCM port can carry more than one SCO channel.)

See PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM_SLOT, PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_CODEC. Also see the QTIL document "BlueCore Audio API Specification", CS-209064-DD.

In devices which support PSKEY_SCO_DATA_PATH, that key may take precedence over this one.

Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to FALSE and TRUE.


PSKEY_HOSTIO_MIN_UART_HCI_SCO_SIZE

Number (psid) 0x01ae 430
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_HOSTIO_MIN_UART_HCI_SCO_SIZE = 30
Allowed Values
Minimum1
Maximum128

Minimum SCO packet size sent to host over UART HCI

A SCO link provides a steady flow of audio samples from air that have to be sent to the host. When SCO data is passed to the host over HCI (i.e., not over the chip's PCM port) the samples have to be formed into HCI SCO packets.

This PSKey sets the minimum number of *samples* in each HCI SCO packet sent to the host over a UART transport - BCSP and H4. (USB has separate rules for defining SCO transport.)

Set this to zero to minimise audio data latency. However this can crowd other data off the host transport. When the available host bandwidth is too low this can block all other traffic, so HCI ACL, HCI CMD/EVT, etc. stop flowing.


PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_CODEC

Number (psid) 0x01b0 432
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
TypeEnumTrueFalse
DefaultPSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_CODEC = FALSE
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
FALSE 0 False
TRUE 1 True

Map SCO over the built-in codec

Some versions of BlueCore include an audio codec, typically used to drive an external microphone and earpiece.

If this PSKey is TRUE, and if PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM is also TRUE, then all SCO connections are routed through the built-in audio codec rather than though the normal PCM interface.

Type bool is fundamentally a uint16 with values 0 and 1 mapping to FALSE and TRUE.


PSKEY_PCM_CVSD_TX_HI_FREQ_BOOST

Number (psid) 0x01b1 433
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB

Allowed Values
Minimum0
Maximum4

High frequency boost for PCM when transmitting CVSD

This PSKey enables a high-frequency emphasis filter used when transmitting voice samples over the radio using CVSD (only used when the host interface is the PCM interface).

Do not alter the default value (disabled) of this PSKey except with specific advice from QTIL. Use of this PSKey is deprecated. It will be removed in a future release of the firmware.

A value of 0 disables the filter. Higher values provide increasing amounts of high frequency boost.

PSKEY_USE_OLD_BCSP_LE

Number (psid) 0x01b4 436
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
Typeboolean
DefaultPSKEY_USE_OLD_BCSP_LE = false
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
false 0
true 1

Use the old version of BCSP link establishment

If this PS Key is set to FALSE then the firmware uses the BCSP Link Establishment protocol described in QTIL document "BCSP Link Establishment Protocol", CS-101681-SP, otherwise it uses the older protocol described in QTIL document bc01-s-010g.

The new protocol was modified to provide a more robust behavior when a host spontaneously reboots or restarts. The new behavior only differs significantly from the old one in that:

- The "choke" is turned off when moving from "curious" to "garrulous".

- The "cnf_cnt_limit" logic is removed; "conf" messages are continuously emitted in the "curious" state.

For detailed descriptions of the state machines and signals see QTIL document "BCSP Link Establishment Protocol", CS-101681-SP.

You may need to set this PSKey to TRUE if the host has an old implementation of BCSP Link Establishment. Old implementations may not support the "garrulous" state.

See PSKEY_BCSP_LM_CNF_CNT_LIMIT.


PSKEY_HOSTIO_SCO_PCM_THRESHOLDS

Number (psid) 0x01bb 443
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
Typeuint16[2]
DefaultPSKEY_HOSTIO_SCO_PCM_THRESHOLDS[ ] = { 8, 20}

Thresholds for SCO PCM buffers

This PSKey sets the upper and lower thresholds for the buffers used to hold SCO data flowing between air and the PCM port.

The thresholds are checked just before a packet is received from air and just after a packet is sent to air.

If the data pending in the buffer exceeds the upper threshold when the level is checked, a sample is deleted from the buffer. If the pending data in the buffer drops below the lower threshold, a sample is inserted into the buffer.

The thresholds are held as a uint16[2]. The first value gives the lower threshold and the second value gives the upper threshold.

This PSKey has no effect on some versions of firmware.


PSKEY_HOSTIO_SCO_HCI_THRESHOLDS

Number (psid) 0x01bc 444
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
Typeuint16[2]
DefaultPSKEY_HOSTIO_SCO_HCI_THRESHOLDS[ ] = { 10, 80}

Thresholds for SCO HCI buffers

This PSKey sets the upper and lower thresholds for the buffers used to hold SCO data flowing between air and the HCI.

The thresholds are checked just before a packet is received from air and just after a packet is sent to air.

When the thresholds are exceeded, the firmware inserts or delete single samples or groups of samples to bring the amount of data pending in the buffer into range. The exact behaviour depends on whether the SCO data is in transparent format and which host transport is in use.

The thresholds are held as a uint16[2]. The first value gives the lower threshold and the second value gives the upper threshold.

This PSKey has no effect on some versions of firmware.


PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM_SLOT

Number (psid) 0x01bd 445
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM_SLOT = 0
Allowed Values
Minimum0
Maximum7

Route SCO data to specified slot in pcm frame

When PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM is TRUE, the first SCO channel opened is routed over the chip's PCM port. While this SCO channel is in place, all subsequent attempts to open extra SCO channels fail.

The SCO channel is routed over the PCM timing frame slot defined by this PSKey. This PSKey's default value, zero, routes to "the first" PCM slot.

The number of slots in the PCM port's timing frame depends on the value of PSKEY_PCM_CONFIG32. For example, there is no use in setting PSKEY_HOSTIO_MAP_SCO_PCM_SLOT to 3, asking for SCO data to travel over the 4th slot in the PCM frame if the PCM channel's clock rate only supports a single slot per frame.

This PSKey is available only in builds for BlueCore2 and later chips. Functionality equivalent to this PSKey is available in BlueCore01b builds using a bit field in PSKEY_PCM_CONFIG, a PSKey absent from builds for BlueCore2 and later chips.

The maximum value for this PSKey is now 7 for BlueCore7-FM, where the upper 4 slots redirect the PCM out of interface 2.

For all previous chips the maximum value is 3.


PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_BCSP

Number (psid) 0x01bf 447
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_UART_CONFIG_BCSP = 0x0806

UART configuration when using BCSP

If PSKEY_HOST_INTERFACE selects BCSP then the UART's configuration register is set to the value of this PSKey when it boots.

The UART configuration register is a bitfield:

Bit Meaning 0 0 => one stop bit, 1 => two stop bits. 1 0 => no parity bits, 1 => one parity bit. 2 0 => odd parity, 1 => even parity. 3 0 => h/w flow control disabled, 1 => enabled. 4 Set to 0. 5 0 => RTS deasserted, 1 => RTS asserted. 6 Set to 0. 7 0 => non-BCSP/H5 operation disabled, 1 => enabled. 8 Set to 0. 9 Set to 0. 10 Set to 0. 11 Set to 1. 12 0 => H5 operation disabled, 1 => enabled. 13 Set to 0. 14 Set to 0. 15 Set to 0.

The default value, 0x0806, selects BCSP mode and even parity.

In builds from HCI 18.X, this key replaces PSKEY_UART_CONFIG, PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_STOP_BITS, PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_PARITY_BIT, PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_FLOW_CTRL_EN, PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_RTS, and PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_NON_BCSP_EN.


PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_H4

Number (psid) 0x01c0 448
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_UART_CONFIG_H4 = 0x08a8

UART configuration when using H4

If PSKEY_HOST_INTERFACE selects H4 then the UART's configuration register is set to the value of this PSKey when it boots.

The UART configuration register is a bitfield and shares its format with PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_BCSP:

Bit Meaning 0 0 => one stop bit, 1 => two stop bits. 1 0 => no parity bits, 1 => one parity bit. 2 0 => odd parity, 1 => even parity. 3 0 => h/w flow control disabled, 1 => enabled. 4 Set to 0. 5 0 => RTS deasserted, 1 => RTS asserted. 6 Set to 0. 7 0 => non-BCSP/H5 operation disabled, 1 => enabled. 8 Set to 0. 9 Set to 0. 10 Set to 0. 11 Set to 1. 12 0 => H5 operation disabled, 1 => enabled. 13 Set to 0. 14 Set to 0. 15 Set to 0.

The default value, 0x08a8, selects use of hardware flow control, as required by the H4 specification.

In builds from HCI 18.X, this key replaces PSKEY_UART_CONFIG, PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_STOP_BITS, PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_PARITY_BIT, PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_FLOW_CTRL_EN, PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_RTS, and PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_NON_BCSP_EN.

CategoryPSKHOSTIOB

DefaultPSKEY_UART_CONFIG_H5 = 0x1806

UART configuration when using H5

If PSKEY_HOST_INTERFACE selects H5 then the UART's configuration register is set to the value of this PSKey when it boots.

The UART configuration register is a bitfield:

Bit Meaning 0 0 => one stop bit, 1 => two stop bits. 1 0 => no parity bits, 1 => one parity bit. 2 0 => odd parity, 1 => even parity. 3 0 => h/w flow control disabled, 1 => enabled. 4 Set to 0. 5 0 => RTS deasserted, 1 => RTS asserted. 6 Set to 0. 7 0 => non-BCSP/H5 operation disabled, 1 => enabled. 8 Set to 0. 9 Set to 0. 10 Set to 0. 11 Set to 1. 12 0 => H5 operation disabled, 1 => enabled. 13 Set to 0. 14 Set to 0. 15 Set to 0.

Note: The "H5" host transport protocol is properly known as the "Three-Wire UART Transport Layer", but is commonly known as H5 within QTIL.

In builds from HCI 18.X, this key replaces PSKEY_UART_CONFIG, PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_STOP_BITS, PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_PARITY_BIT, PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_FLOW_CTRL_EN, PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_RTS, and PSKEY_UART_CONFIG_NON_BCSP_EN.

PSKEY_UART_TX_CRCS

Number (psid) 0x01c3 451
CategoryPSKHOSTIOB
Typeboolean
DefaultPSKEY_UART_TX_CRCS = true
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
false 0

Use CRCs for BCSP or H5

This PSKey determines whether CRCs are used in BCSP packets sent to the host.
