PSKEY_AGC_RSSI_THRESHOLD_BREDR

Number (psid) 0x2741 10049
CategoryPSKSYSB5
Typeint8
DefaultPSKEY_AGC_RSSI_THRESHOLD_BREDR = -80 dBm
Allowed Values
Minimum-128 dBm
Maximum127 dBm

BR/EDR RSSI threshold for AGC gain switching

When the system is selecting AGC settings automatically depending on historic information, the value of this key controls the received signal strength at which the gain is switched for BR/EDR links. Keys PSKEY_AGC_PREFERENCE_INQUIRY_SCAN and PSKEY_AGC_PREFERENCE_INQUIRY control the gains to be used in situations where there is no historic information.

This key is in units of dBm.

Setting this key to -128 dBm will effectively disable switching and keep the system permanently on the lower current, poorer sensitivity settings. Setting this key to +127 dBm will keep the system permanently on the higher current, better sensitivity settings.

Note that there is no key to control the threshold for paging, a different technique is used. See the documentation of PSKEY_AGC_PREFERENCE_INQUIRY and PSKEY_AGC_PREFERENCE_INQUIRY_SCAN for the reason.

This setting can also be dynamically configured via the bccmd interface using the command BCCMD_AGC_RSSI_THRESHOLD.

Allowed Values
Minimum-128 dBm
Maximum127 dBm

Keys PSKEY_AGC_PREFERENCE_ADVERTISING and PSKEY_AGC_PREFERENCE_LE_SCAN control the gains to be used in situations where there is no historic information.

This key is in units of dBm.

Setting this key to -128 dBm will effectively disable switching and keep the system permanently on the lower current, poorer sensitivity settings. Setting this key to +127 dBm will keep the system permanently on the higher current, better sensitivity settings.

PSKEY_AGC_PREFERENCE_INQUIRY_SCAN

Number (psid) 0x2744 10052
CategoryPSKSYSB5
TypeEnumAgcOptions
DefaultPSKEY_AGC_PREFERENCE_INQUIRY_SCAN = AGC_LOWER_CURRENT
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
AGC_LOWER_CURRENT 0 Prefer lower current at the cost of reduced sensitivity
AGC_BETTER_SENSITIVITY 1 Prefer better sensitivity at the cost of higher current

Preferred AGC settings for inquiry scan

This key controls the AGC gain settings to be used during inquiry scan. During inquiry scan there is no historic information about the expected signal strength for a reception but inquiry scan uses the receiver for extended periods of time so can be an operation in which current consumption can be significant.

The recommendation is to use the lower current, poorer sensitivity settings here as in the receptions performed for inquiry scan all that is being received is an ID packet. ID packets have significant processing gain. If it's not possible to detect ID packets with the lower AGC settings then it's likely a real link will be unstable even using the higher gain settings.

For the same reason, there is no equivalent key for page scan. For page scan the lower current, poorer sensitivity settings are used for the initial ID packet reception but the system automatically steps up to the higher current, better sensitivity settings for the FHS packet reception and the start of the link. These subsequent stages of connection formation are rare and so the overall system current penalty for always using the better sensitivity settings is negligible. Once the connection is formed the RSSI will be tracked and the gain settings adjusted as appropriate according to the setting in PSKEY_AGC_RSSI_THRESHOLD_BREDR.

This setting can also be dynamically configured via the bccmd interface using the command BCCMD_AGC_PREFERENCE.


PSKEY_AGC_PREFERENCE_INQUIRY

Number (psid) 0x2745 10053
CategoryPSKSYSB5
TypeEnumAgcOptions
DefaultPSKEY_AGC_PREFERENCE_INQUIRY = AGC_LOWER_CURRENT
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
AGC_LOWER_CURRENT 0 Prefer lower current at the cost of reduced sensitivity
AGC_BETTER_SENSITIVITY 1 Prefer better sensitivity at the cost of higher current

Preferred AGC settings for inquiry

This key controls the AGC gain settings to be used during inquiry. During inquiry there is no historic information about the expected signal strength for a reception but inquiry uses the receiver for extended periods of time so can be an operation in which current consumption can be significant.

The best setting to use here is a whole system decision. Unlike in inquiry scan, page scan and page the first packet that's being received has a payload so the processing gain is marginal (although there is some as it's an FHS packet using FEC 2/3 encoding). Hence on the lower current, poorer sensitivity settings there's a small risk of being unable to detect inquiry responses from devices to which it would be possible to connect. If the whole system performs inquiry only rarely but wants to discover devices at the limit of range then the higher current, better sensitivity settings will avoid this risk at only a negligible increase in current. If the whole system performs inquiry frequently or is not concerned about devices at the limit of range then the lower current, poorer sensitivity settings will be fine.

Note that there is no equivalent key for paging. The initial packet reception during paging is an ID packet which has significant processing gain. If that packet can't be received on the lower current, poorer sensitivity settings then it is likely that it will not be possible to form or maintain a connection even with the higher current, better sensitivity settings. Once the system receives the first ID packet it automatically switches to the higher current, better sensitivity settings for the rest of connection formation. These later stages are rare so the overall system current consumption impact of using the higher sensitivity settings is negligible. Once the connection is formed the RSSI will be tracked and the gain settings adjusted as appropriate according to the setting in PSKEY_AGC_RSSI_THRESHOLD_BREDR.

This setting can also be dynamically configured via the bccmd interface using the command BCCMD_AGC_PREFERENCE.


PSKEY_AGC_PREFERENCE_ADVERTISING

Number (psid) 0x2746 10054
CategoryPSKSYSB5
TypeEnumAgcOptions
DefaultPSKEY_AGC_PREFERENCE_ADVERTISING = AGC_LOWER_CURRENT
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
AGC_LOWER_CURRENT 0 Prefer lower current at the cost of reduced sensitivity
AGC_BETTER_SENSITIVITY 1 Prefer better sensitivity at the cost of higher current

Preferred AGC settings for advertising

This key controls the AGC gain settings to be used during advertising, including advertising done as part of forming a connection. During advertising there is no historic information about the expected signal strength for a reception but inquiry uses the receiver for extended periods of time so can be an operation in which current consumption can be significant.

The best setting to use here is a whole system decision. If the whole system performs advertises only rarely but wants to discover and connect to devices at the limit of range then the higher current, better sensitivity settings will avoid this risk. Whether the current consumption increase with these settings is significant depends what fraction of its battery life the device spends advertising. If the whole system performs advertising frequently or is not concerned about devices at the limit of range then the lower current, poorer sensitivity settings will be a better choice.

For multi-stage operations, like receiving a scan response or connecting then once the first packet has been received the system will automatically step up to the higher current, better sensitivity setting. These later stages are rare so the overall system current consumption impact of using the higher sensitivity settings is negligible. If a connection is formed the RSSI will be tracked and the gain settings adjusted as appropriate according to the setting in PSKEY_AGC_RSSI_THRESHOLD_1LE or PSKEY_AGC_RSSI_THRESHOLD_2LE.

Note that this key is irrelevant for non-connectable advertising as the local device does not attempt to receive during that operation.

This setting can also be dynamically configured via the bccmd interface using the command BCCMD_AGC_PREFERENCE.


PSKEY_AGC_PREFERENCE_LE_SCAN

Preferred AGC settings for LE scan

This key controls the AGC gain settings to be used during LE scanning operations, including scanning done as part of forming a connection. During scanning there is no historic information about the expected signal strength for a reception but inquiry uses the receiver for extended periods of time so can be an operation in which current consumption can be significant.

The best setting to use here is a whole system decision. If the whole system scans only rarely but wants to be discovered by and connect to devices at the limit of range then the higher current, better sensitivity settings will avoid this risk. Whether the current consumption increase with these settings is significant depends what fraction of its battery life the device spends advertising. If the whole system performs scanning frequently or is not concerned about devices at the limit of range then the lower current, poorer sensitivity settings will be a better choice.

For multi-stage operations, most notably forming a connection, then once the first packet has been received the system will automatically step up to the higher current, better sensitivity setting. These later stages are rare so the overall system current consumption impact of using the higher sensitivity settings is negligible. If a connection is formed the RSSI will be tracked and the gain settings adjusted as appropriate according to the setting in PSKEY_AGC_RSSI_THRESHOLD_1LE or PSKEY_AGC_RSSI_THRESHOLD_2LE.

This setting can also be dynamically configured via the bccmd interface using the command BCCMD_AGC_PREFERENCE.

PSKEY_TX_POWER_TEMPERATURE_COMPENSATION

Number (psid) 0x2749 10057
CategoryPSKSYSB5
Typetemperature_calibration[ ]
DefaultPSKEY_TX_POWER_TEMPERATURE_COMPENSATION[ ] = {{ -40 /* absolute */, -3 /* internal */}, \
{ 25 /* absolute */, 0 /* internal */}}

Compensation of BR TX power for temperature

This key consists of pairs of 16-bit signed values. The first is a temperature, the second a compensation value used at that temperature. The temperatures should increase monotonically, but the corrections at each temperature needn't. Values are interpolated between temperatures and extended beyond the range if necessary.

This key applies to basic rate and Bluetooth Low Energy (BLE) transmit power.

The table length is not fixed and should have the required number of pairs of values.

Note that interpolation means that if a step of more than one is desired then adjacent temperatures will need to appear in the table.

See also PSKEY_TX_POWER_TEMPERATURE_COMPENSATION2.


PSKEY_TX_POWER_COMPENSATION_N_ROWS

Number (psid) 0x274a 10058
CategoryPSKSYSB5
Typeuint16
DefaultPSKEY_TX_POWER_COMPENSATION_N_ROWS = 1

Number of power table rows to compensate

This key specifies the number of rows starting from the highest power of the power table to apply temperature compensation to.

The key will only have any effect if the corresponding compensation coefficients have been set: PSKEY_TX_POWER_TEMPERATURE_COMPENSATION for Basic Rate and BLE, and PSKEY_TX_POWER_TEMPERATURE_COMPENSATION2 for EDR.

PSKEY_LE_PHY_POLICY_SWITCH_POINTS

Number (psid) 0x274d 10061
CategoryPSKSYSB5
Typeuint16[ ]
DefaultPSKEY_LE_PHY_POLICY_SWITCH_POINTS[ ] = { 2, 1}

Configures the 2LE <-> 1LE switch

This key only does anything if PSKEY_LE_PHY_POLICY = 1.

This key controls the switch points for the 2LE <-> 1LE switch when autonomous PHY updates are enabled.

It has the form {X,Y} where X = switch point from 2LE to 1LE. We switch at 0.02% BER. Y = switch point from 1LE to 2LE. We switch at 0.01% BER.

PSKEY_LDO_OFFSET_CAL_PARAMS

Number (psid) 0x2757 10071
CategoryPSKSYSB5
Typeldo_offset_cal_params
DefaultPSKEY_LDO_OFFSET_CAL_PARAMS = { 300 /* meas_dac */, 389 /* ctap_volt_meas_dac_min */, 492 /* ctap_volt_meas_dac_max */}

Parameters for LDO offset calibration

This key provides the input for the LDO offset calibration. It includes the following in the respective order:

meas_dac - AM DAC value at which the measurements are done. ctap_volt_meas_dac_min - Balun center tap (min) req for meas_dac. ctap_volt_meas_dac_max - Balun center tap (max) req for meas_dac.

The ctap voltage is represented in volts, scaled by 2^10 (for example, 380 mV is represented numerically as 389).After calibration it is expected that the measured voltage with AM DAC at meas_dac will be in the range [ctap_volt_meas_dac_min, ctap_volt_meas_dac_max].

This key is for Qualcomm internal use only and must not be altered.

PSKEY_AMAM_LO_USE_FM

Number (psid) 0x275a 10074
CategoryPSKSYSB5
TypeEnumTrueFalse
DefaultPSKEY_AMAM_LO_USE_FM = TRUE
Allowed Values
Defined name Value Description
FALSE 0 False
TRUE 1 True

Spread the LO channel during AMAM calibration

During the AMAM calibration the device will emit RF centered on the channel specified by PSKEY_IQ_TRIM_CHANNEL. If this key is set to True the LO will be modulated to spread the RF, and the calibration is then less susceptible to ambient noise.

This key controls radio operation. Do not alter it.
